  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_be102733-1162-48da-9d26-bf700365427f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer15120325923160838232">Where do you go when nowhere is safe?<br/><br/>Sixteen years after a deadly virus wiped out most of Earth's population, the world is a perilous place.   <span id="freeText15120325923160838232" style="display:none">Where do you go when nowhere is safe?<br /><br />Sixteen years after a deadly virus wiped out most of Earth's population, the world is a perilous place. Eighteen-year-old Eve has never been beyond the heavily guarded perimeter of her school, where she and two hundred other orphaned girls have been promised a future as the teachers and artists of the New America. But the night before graduation, Eve learns the shocking truth about her school's real purpose and the horrifying fate that awaits her.<br /><br />Fleeing the only home she's ever known, Eve sets off on a long, treacherous journey, searching for a place she can survive. Along the way she encounters Arden, her former rival from school, and Caleb, a rough, rebellious boy living in the wild. Separated from men her whole life, Eve has been taught to fear them, but Caleb slowly wins her trust... and her heart. He promises to protect her, but when soldiers begin hunting them, Eve must choose between true love and her life. <br /><br />In this epic new series, Anna Carey imagines a future that is both beautiful and terrifying.</span>

    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241426448?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11345832-eve">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241426448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11994546542378821887"><b>Instant Dystopia: <i>Now With 50% Less Logic!</i></b><br/><br/>Start with your randomly selected future date at room temperature. Add an ambiguous <b>Plague</b> (capitalised is best). Stir briefly to create a drastic population reduction, thereby ensuring wombs are a hot commodity in your new society. Heavily indoctrinate your characters to keep them in line and create exploitative scenarios, especially for teenagers. Insert an <b>Improbable and Unexplained System of Government</b>. <br/><br/>Got <b>Plausibility Problems</b>? Just add <b>Romance</b>! (I</span>
  <span id="freeText11994546542378821887" style="display:none"><b>Instant Dystopia: <i>Now With 50% Less Logic!</i></b><br><br>Start with your randomly selected future date at room temperature. Add an ambiguous <b>Plague</b> (capitalised is best). Stir briefly to create a drastic population reduction, thereby ensuring wombs are a hot commodity in your new society. Heavily indoctrinate your characters to keep them in line and create exploitative scenarios, especially for teenagers. Insert an <b>Improbable and Unexplained System of Government</b>. <br><br>Got <b>Plausibility Problems</b>? Just add <b>Romance</b>! (Instant or QuickLuv is recommended). Sprinkle with <i>Yearning Gazes, Electrifying Touches</i> and <i>Heaving Breaths</i> to taste. Season liberally with <b>Tension</b>, or better yet, add <b>Love Triangle</b> and bring to the boil. <br><br>Insert <b>Cliffhanger</b>. <br><br>Huzzah! You have an <b>Instant Dystopia</b>! Plate up with a pretty cover (Shiny Locks and Flowing Dress optional). Serve while this trend is still hot!<br>~<br><br>Oh, Eve. Where do I start? <br><br><a href="http://s1130.photobucket.com/albums/m523/reynje/?action=view&amp;current=dystopian-future_design.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364067i/715602.png" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Despite a promising, albeit somewhat unoriginal, premise – it all went horribly wrong for me when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11345832.Eve__The_Eve_Trilogy___1_" title="Eve (The Eve Trilogy, #1) by Anna Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Eve</a> climbed aboard the Trope Train and didn’t know when to get off. Rushing straight past the stops of “frighteningly plausible” and “sound world building”, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11345832.Eve__The_Eve_Trilogy___1_" title="Eve (The Eve Trilogy, #1) by Anna Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Eve</a> charges down the well-travelled tracks of tru luv, flimsy backstory and convenient yet improbable scenarios. Throw in a thoroughly unsympathetic heroine and a head-desk inducing cliffhanger, and the resultant wreck claimed a few rating stars as casualties, along with my interest in reading the sequel. <br><br>One of the major issues I had with this book (I’ll get to the biggest in a minute) was the version of a “dystopian” world Carey presents. The scaffolding holding this world up was simply too rickety to stand up under questioning. We’re presented with an unexplained plague that has almost depleted the population, and a rigid system of schools and labour camps funnelling the remaining youth into sinister service to the “King of the New America”. Which for girls means, you guessed it, forced breeding. (Is it just me, or is this “girl’s value is in their baby producing ability” topic coming up a lot lately?)<br><br>Very little is provided in the way of explanation to flesh out this bleak vision of the future. I was distracted by this thinness of the world building throughout, struggling to visualise and accept the set up at face value. (And an immature inclination to chortle at the mention of the “King”.)<br><br>But the crux of my disengagement from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11345832.Eve__The_Eve_Trilogy___1_" title="Eve (The Eve Trilogy, #1) by Anna Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Eve</a> was Eve herself. I cannot recall a recent YA heroine that I have more vehemently disliked than this girl, who spends the entire book lurching from selfish decision to selfish decision. This in itself was perplexing to me. Although she was raised in a cloistered school with no contact with the outside world, and is actively educated in the “evils” of men and love, Eve purportedly has close friends of several years, and ample opportunity build meaningful relationships with her peers. <br><br>Despite this, Eve seems to have little compulsion to act in a compassionate or thoughtful manner, instead being so absorbed in herself that she causes harm to those around her. Further, Eve’s drastic flip-flop from fear of being raped to being basically affronted that she was not her rescuer’s “type”, was infuriating, not to mention ridiculous. <br><br>Granted, Eve has no understanding of how to survive in the wild, due to the closeted world she has been raised in. However, Eve’s continued abandonment, ignorance and outright endangerment of those around her boggled my mind. She leaves a trail of destruction in her wake as she stumbles through this story, and I simply couldn’t find it in myself to sympathise with her. On the contrary, I was frustrated, annoyed and entirely uninterested in her pity-parties. By the time she actually took pause to reflect on exactly what kind of havoc she had wreaked, I was so disconnected from her as a character that it was a struggle to muster any interest in her self-analysis. <br><br>Conversely, Eve’s former schoolmate and fellow escapee, Arden, was a girl I warmed to. Although initially cast as the suspicious outsider/mean girl, she was straight-talking, tough and intelligent, and frequently had scenes that made me want slap her a high-five. <br><br>The romance aspect of this story fell equally flat for me. Commencing when Caleb rescues Eve from an imminent bear attack, the two inevitably exchange meaningful gazes and heart-pounding touches. While I didn’t dislike Caleb as a character, and the life he and the other orphaned boys lived was somewhat intriguing, there was too much here that felt contrived and implausible. Not the least of this was the ease with which Eve assimilates into their world. Years of propaganda, fear and manipulation by her Teachers are swept away in mere days. Half-wild boys comport themselves, for the most part, like mild mannered school boys. And naturally, Eve falls in “love” with her dreadlocked, “ball song” singing saviour.<br><br>I can’t even write about Leif here, and the situation that unfolds during the raid, because I’m afraid I’ll punch my computer. <br><br>Below is a visual representation of my like or dislike of the main characters, relative to some of the major events. (Within a spoiler due to the naming of plot points):<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <a href="http://s1130.photobucket.com/albums/m523/reynje/?action=view&amp;current=graph-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364067i/715603._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>On the positive side, Carey’s writing is fluid and holds attention, and she changes up the scenery and events regularly enough to keep the story well paced. It’s a fairly swift read, with a plot that keeps turning consistently. <br> <br>Yet, just when I was beginning to soften, beginning to feel some interest in what would become of the characters and feel an investment in their goal: <i>the ending</i>. Although it is rather in keeping with the way Eve has behaved throughout the entire preceding story, it still seemed illogical and out of place to me. Frankly, it felt like the entire slog through Eve’s story was met with a slap in the face, and a cheap ploy to generate investment in the sequel. <br><br>However, I’m sincere when I say that I hope the continuation of this trilogy gets stronger. I certainly hope more of the world is explained and detailed. I hope some of the minor characters play a larger role, as there is real potential for their stories to be interesting. <br><br>That said, the bear is still my favourite character. High five, Bear!<br><br><a href="http://s1130.photobucket.com/albums/m523/reynje/?action=view&amp;current=high-five-bear.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364067i/715604.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_186655073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186655073" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186655073?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186655073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer338395003914571736"><i>”He was a strange breed of man, part wild. Not the sophisticated kind who graced the pages of The Great Gatsby. Nor did he seem like the violent man I’d encountered on my first day in the wild. He had saved me, at least. I could only hope that it wasn’t for some nefarious purpose.”</i><br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>The idea…. I know people will be like ‘B-b-but it’s exactly the same as The Handmaid’s Tale’… but I’ve never read it sooo… I think Ms Carey did a great job at setting up this idea and it was incredibly cree</span>
  <span id="freeText338395003914571736" style="display:none"><i>”He was a strange breed of man, part wild. Not the sophisticated kind who graced the pages of The Great Gatsby. Nor did he seem like the violent man I’d encountered on my first day in the wild. He had saved me, at least. I could only hope that it wasn’t for some nefarious purpose.”</i><br><br><b>High Points.</b><br>The idea…. I know people will be like ‘B-b-but it’s exactly the same as The Handmaid’s Tale’… but I’ve never read it sooo… I think Ms Carey did a great job at setting up this idea and it was incredibly creepy. Arden. Caleb post-Eve. Ruby &amp; Pip. Lief post-Eve. <br><br><b>Low Points.</b><br>Eve. <br>This book would have been <i>awesome</i> if Eve had just called in sick. <br>The representation of men. If you have a penis in this book you have to either be a leery sexual predator or a boy who goes all gooey when there is a girl in your vicinity. MAKE YOUR CHOICE, BOYS.<br>Insta-love. Can you buy this in a can? I think it is only acceptable (ish) for authors to make their characters fall in love so quickly in stand-alone novels. If you know that your book is going to be a series… let it simmer for a bit. You’ll make your readers go <i>mental</i>. <br>When they get together in like the fourth chapter, the mystery is gone and, unfortunately, so is my interest. <br>I really hope this is one of those series that gets better, because this book does have potential but these creases need to be ironed out. <br><br><b>Heroine.</b><br>I have a lot in common with <s>Mary Sue</s> Eve: she’s beautiful, she’s intelligent, she’s irresistible to boys and she’s innocent and thinks that when a boy refers to his *whispers* <i>balls</i> he means the balls on his foot. (I <i>still</i> don’t get that joke. Sigh.)<br>She’s also a complete and utter Annoying Female Protagonist. (AFP)<br>I don’t want to be too cruel because it’s not entirely her fault. She’s had it pretty rough. She’s had to grow up without a mother in an all-girls school and a PLAGUE has killed everyone else, so her naivety and nervousness when it comes to the male species is understandable.<br>Because all girls who go to an all-girls school get jumpy and skittish when people of the male disposition are nearby. I mean, when I went to sixth form and a boy sat down next to me I stabbed him in the thigh with my fountain pen because his foot touched mine. <br>She’s never even <i>seen</i> a boy, so you can imagine what she’s like when Caleb and his glistening muscles and his whip (not joking) rides into her life (literally, on a stallion) after saving her from a bear (Yeah.. that happens).<br>It doesn’t help that she also had to attend "Dangers of Boys and Men" seminars (Um, yeah… that happens too.)<br>So I can let her off in that respect, albeit a little reluctantly. Because she has an excuse.<br>What she <i>doesn’t</i> have an excuse for is sashaying around <s>Neverland</s> the underground hovel in her skimpy clothes and wondering why the boys (who have never seen a girl either) are ogling at her goodies and then getting her kecks in a twist about it. Woman, just put a fleece on or something. <br>And neither does she have an excuse for going on about how amazing her best friends are/were. Um, well… if they’re so fun and amazing and always there for you even if you are annoying, then why did you leave them to get Atwood-ed?! Eh?<br>Also, you’re a reet Moaning Minnie.<br>But other than that…..<br><br><b>Best Friend.</b><br>I feel really sorry for Eve’s friends. They seem really sweet, funny and very patient with Eve’s AFP ways. One of them also sings <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ajCYQL8ouqw" rel="nofollow noopener">my second favourite Beatles song </a> in the shower. So that’s also fine. <br>But yeah… I’m hoping Pip and Ruby get more air time in the other books because they were great and grossly under-used. I also am hankering for a show-down between them where they just beat Eve with a stick for leaving them high and dry and getting distracted by abs instead of helping them. <br>Also, major love for Arden. She is rebellious and prickly and has a personality and cut her hair short because she doesn’t care what people think of her. <br>I also thought that she was going to be the obstacle between Eve and Caleb’s undying love because she perved at him when she first saw him. And I got all excited because it’s far more likely for two girls to fight over a boy than two boys over a girl. And I thought “Wow, that’s different and exciting and unique”.<br>But before I could say “CATFIGHT!!” it was made clear that Caleb only has eyes for Eve. <i>So that was the end of that.</i><br><br><b>Love Interest.</b><br>It’s difficult to not to swoon over a boy like Caleb. He’s ripped as anything, he walks around topless, he has edgy and unique hair, he’s sweet, he doesn’t gawk at Eve’s boobs and he’s a bit feral. Perfect guy, right?<br><i>Well.</i><br>You know when someone tells you not to think of something and all you can do is think of that thing?<br>This is how I pictured Caleb. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353496i/706838.jpg" width="300" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, don’t get me wrong. I love Rufio as much as the next girl and what happens to him <i>always</i> shocks me because I have selective memory with things like that and I pretend it doesn’t happen. <br>But bringer of the swoon he is not.<br>Caleb has potential to develop into a BotS in future books… if he drops the ball and chain…. Off a cliff.<br>Also, unlike Eve, whose too polite and in love with you and describes your smell as ‘earthy’ and ‘smokey’ and ‘charcoaly’, I am <i>not</i> polite and in love with you so I substituted these pleasant adjective with my own phrase - "gross boy smell". <br>Which is more likely because you’ve been living <i>underground</i> with other smelly boys for years.<br>Also, it made these descriptions HILARIOUS. <br><blockquote>
<br>“His gaze traced the lines of my mouth, his eyes finally settling on mine. His breath filled my ears and I smelled the <s>charcoal</s> <b>gross boy smell</b> again as I leaned closer.”</blockquote><br><br>See?<br><br><b>Baddie.</b><br>Hmm… I’m reluctant to put Lief in this category because I’m guessing he’s going to swagger into the above category as the series continues. But yeah, he’s a massive douchebag and he can’t control his animal urges but he also has <i>issues</i> and a <i>sensitive</i> side.<br>And he’s totally smokin’.<br>Also we have the King. But we didn’t find much about him, except that he must have Eve. <br>And then we have THE PLAGUE. But unless I missed the part that explains anything about what this PLAGUE is or why it killed 98% of the world’s population… we’re going to have to wait for book two to find out about this.<br>I’m still holding out for the 98% of the world’s population to suddenly re-animate and eat everyone. And when I say everyone… I mostly mean Eve, because I was fond of all the other characters. <br><br><br><b>Theme Tune.</b><br><br><i>Dear Eve,<br><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6inwzOooXRU" rel="nofollow noopener">This song is for you,</a><br>Best Wishes,<br>Everybody in New America. </i><br><br>Also, <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wsdy_rct6uo&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">this song </a>is for Caleb to serenade Eve with when she realises she actually <i>does</i> fancy the hottie with the frisky hands in future books. <br>This song is the only instant where love triangles are fun. And I think Caleb would suit one of those chunky knits.<br>But I have a feeling that those aren’t diamonds in his pocket…<br><br><b>Angst Level.</b><br>5/10. The reason why Eve escaped from school is really grim and terrifying to think of. But apart from that and the occasional Handy McGrabby boy, this book is pretty tame in the angst section.<br>There are many pages where we get Eve whinging about the repercussions of the situations she got herself into. And, of course, boy angst. <br>Because she’s stoopid. <br><br><b>Recommended for.</b><br>People who have hope that some series get better as they go on. People who love dystopian fiction in all its oppressive ways. People who ever thought “You know what? I wish this story had more boys who don’t know the meaning of ‘look don’t touch’” about Peter Pan. People who don’t read the word ‘plague’ and automatically get excited over the prospect of potential zombies. People who think Rufio has some kind of, allure. People who are going to have to watch Hook so they can make an informed decision. <br><br><br><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers, it will be available to buy later this year. </i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="338395003914571736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241048962?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241048962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2605130232819605713">well, this is very telling.<br/><br/>i came over here to write the review for this book, and realized i couldn't find my copy of it. "no worries," i thought, "i will just write the review from my recollections of the text without using any quotes or anything..."<br/><br/>crickets.<br/><br/>it's not that i don't have any memories of it—i do: innocence, arden, breeding, bear, radio, wild boys, freckles, pantry, bridge, love.<br/><br/>there. that's a review, right?<br/><br/>the book is fine, it just suffers from being <strong>ONE MORE</strong> in an already crazy-</span>
  <span id="freeText2605130232819605713" style="display:none">well, this is very telling.<br><br>i came over here to write the review for this book, and realized i couldn't find my copy of it. "no worries," i thought, "i will just write the review from my recollections of the text without using any quotes or anything..."<br><br>crickets.<br><br>it's not that i don't have any memories of it—i do: innocence, arden, breeding, bear, radio, wild boys, freckles, pantry, bridge, love.<br><br>there. that's a review, right?<br><br>the book is fine, it just suffers from being <strong>ONE MORE</strong> in an already crazy-long line of books just like it. and i think this is the kind of book elizabeth was talking about the other day when she said YA exhausts her because she is tired of reading another cheesy teen love story, just with different scenery. or something. she said it better—i forget where. i just went looking for it, and ended up getting distracted by new reviews and comments and then remembered—oh, yeah, i am supposed to be writing a book review.<br><br>so you see how into writing this review i am.<br><br>i thought it started out fine. (the book, not the review—that was a disaster from the get-go) i liked the premise even though i don't totally buy the character: so eve has been sheltered in her girl-cocoon; friend to all, golden child, star pupil, ace reporter, and then just out of the clear blue sky, because some teen rebel tells her something shocking, yes, but something that goes against everything eve "knows," she's just gonna break one of the most fundamental rules of her society and go stumbling across the water even though she can't even swim, putting herself in danger just on the strength of a quick convo with a chick she doesn't even <i>like</i>? it just seems like someone indoctrinated into that world would be less <em>investigative</em>, you know?<br><br>but i guess that is part of what makes eve <strong>SPECIAL!</strong><br><br>but she's not. not really. i personally am tired of selfishness being passed off as naïveté. eve is not a heroine. she is the main protagonist, but she has no honor. so many people come to bad ends because of her actions, and she is just swanning through the wreckage, unscathed, in her revealing clothing cooing, "what are these <i>boys</i> and why are they all <i>looking</i> at me??"<br><br>backtrack. eve has been raised in an all-girl environment, been told that men are all horrible rapists and that once she gets her shiny education, she will go to the golden land and live a life of academic bliss and personal happiness. but that's a lie, and after all the intensive schooling, all these girls are just going to be strapped to a bed and forced to make baby after baby for the brave new world.<br><br>wait—so why are they trained so well? it's not as though these girls are going to be raising their babies and passing along this education, so no one is going to benefit from this schooling at all. seems a waste of time and resources.<br><br>so whatever—eve escapes, leaving behind her closest friends, not warning them that they are about to become baby-machines, hot on the heels of teen rebel arden who told her the truth in the first place. of course they are going to somehow meet up in the great wide world. and of course there are going to be boys.<br><br>so eve gets rescued from a bear (oooooh, cuddly!!) by a dreadlocked boy on a stallion, and he takes her back to his little lost boys enclave, where the younger boys crouch at her feet and learn how to read, and the older boys stifle their lust, with varying degrees of success.<br><br>because this is a YA novel, we will not be picky about the realty of this situation. dirty boys, living in the wilderness, with no former dealings with women are probably not going to be standing on ceremony here. i think it would have gotten uglier in a real-world situation.<br><br>but not here. here it is a relatively safe place where only one boy loses his self control and another boy gets to experience troo love.<br><br>and eve gets to ruin a few more lives.<br><br>later, she will do something else stupid (<strong>FOR LOOOOVE</strong>) and ruin a few more. irrevocably.<br><br>and we aren't going to talk about how adaptable eve seems to be, from being told for 18 years that all men are bad to only showing a little bit of initial fear that is pretty quickly sloughed off as she takes charge and falls into insta-love.<br><br>but she has to keep running, because the king wants to put his own personal baby in her because she is the most beautiful and the most dumb.<br><br>and the ending. oh, dear. it is the most abrupt ending in the history of books. i am going to avoid spoilers but it's like, "oh, wait, what?? really?? but i love you. oh, okay, whatever. see ya"<br><br>end book.<br><br>i know i kind of trashed the book here, but it is not the worst thing i have read. i was interested enough to keep reading, and the concept was good, if some of the world-building elements were far-fetched and counterintuitive. but it is fun and quick, and who needs plausibility, right?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2605130232819605713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162427241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162427241" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162427241?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11345832-eve">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Not sure, but I enjoyed it</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      I did
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable">it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=what-kind-of-ending-was-that">what-kind-of-ending-was-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=poor-world-building">poor-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=all-the-wrong-choices">all-the-wrong-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=heroines-i-want-to-shake">heroines-i-want-to-shake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162427241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13048771275144870563"><br/>One of the first questions I ask myself when I'm reading a dystopian novel is, "Could I ever live in this world?" I can easily answer no for <i>Eve</i>. I can see this book having two distinctive effects on people: horrifying them and completely turning them off or intriguing them just enough to keep them reading. I'm happy to say I fell in the latter category.<br/><br/>Eve lives in a world that has been devastated by a deadly Plague leaving countless children orphans. As a result, the country is in disorder and</span>
  <span id="freeText13048771275144870563" style="display:none"><br>One of the first questions I ask myself when I'm reading a dystopian novel is, "Could I ever live in this world?" I can easily answer no for <i>Eve</i>. I can see this book having two distinctive effects on people: horrifying them and completely turning them off or intriguing them just enough to keep them reading. I'm happy to say I fell in the latter category.<br><br>Eve lives in a world that has been devastated by a deadly Plague leaving countless children orphans. As a result, the country is in disorder and the people, desperate for a solution, allowing one man to rule as king, whose ideals for rebuilding, prey on the most innocent members of society. Girls, or sows, are sent to Schools where they are taught men are evil and manipulative only to graduate and be forced to conceive child after child to help populate the world. Boys, on the other hand, are sent to labor camps where they work long hours, their innocence stolen before it even had time to begin. Eve learns these awful truths the day before she is set to graduate and she does what anyone in her situation would do. She runs.<br><br><b>Things I loved</b><br><br>The premise of the book is a disturbing one. Connecting with the minor characters was something I didn't expect would happen. I couldn't help but think of my own children as I read it. To think society would ever slip that far and abuse our children...it bothers me. It bothered me on the same level that the <i>Hunger Games</i> did with children battling it out to the death for adult entertainment. So, for that <i>Eve</i> kept me turning page after page because as a mother my heart broke for the kids in this book. There was one scene in the book were a little boy asks Eve what love is and she tells them:<blockquote>
  <i>"Love is just caring for someone very deeply. Feeling like that person matters to you, like your whole world would be sadder without them in it."</i>
</blockquote>That was just very heartbreaking for me. For a 6-year-old not knowing what love is. Like I said, it bothers me. But not in the bad way where I would want to stop reading. Instead, in a way that made me stop and be very thankful for what I have in life. <br><br>The writing style was pretty good, in my opinion. I could even pick out a few quotes that I thought were lovely like this one: <blockquote>
  <i>The stream was the only hand that touched me, the wind the only breath that blew the dust from my eyes. I learned the strange art of loneliness, the weathered yearning that swells and passes, swells and passes, when you walk a trail alone.</i>
</blockquote>I also really liked the love interest, Caleb. You know how the love interest always pulls the card where his controlling over protectiveness is romanticized as loving concern? I didn't find that here. Caleb was a sweet guy. He took care of Eve and her friend, Arden when they had nowhere to go. I could feel that he really cared for Eve. There is one part of the novel that spoke volumes about his character to me. Eve was staying with Caleb and a group of other "stray" boys and they were just about to go on a raid the guard’s outpost. Caleb doesn't think it's a good idea that she goes:<blockquote>
  <i>"What if I still want to go?"<br>"Then you'll go," he said. "But I wanted you to know the danger."</i>
</blockquote>That quote made me so happy because YES, let's tell the heroine of the danger, but YES, let <i>her</i> decide if she wants to proceed or not. <br><br><b>Things I disliked</b><br><br>I think we all saw this coming from me: The world building. Unfortunately, I had trouble with the believability that America could sink so low as to do away with democracy, liberty, and basic human rights in such a short amount of time. It's only been sixteen years and Americans have reverted to enslaving their children? No, just no. Furthermore, if the goal is to reproduce as fast as humanly possible, why aren't the adults (who live comfortably in the city) charged with having children? Why only the orphan girls? Not only that, but again, and this seems to be something I'm saying a lot lately, but what in the world are the rest of the human population doing? <br><br>Besides that sketchy world building, there was one big thing that I really disliked: Eve. Eve had exactly three "modes" in this book: 1)Saw dust for brains 2)Too stupid to live 3)Selfish. She goes through the novel making the worst decisions possible that either ended up getting someone else hurt or killed. I get that she was sheltered all her life and that perception of the real world had been tampered with, but why no common sense? Petting a wild bear is suicide. It does not in any way, shape, or form resemble Winnie the Pooh. It's time for a wild life lesson:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348679i/702873._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you saw a grizzly in the woods, would you immediately think of this guy?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348679i/702874.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Maybe I'm missing something here. Do they look related to you? No? Not even distant cousins, twice removed? Now, I'm no expert, but to me it looks like one of these bears is about to rip a clueless girl a new one, while the other is only a danger to himself of overdosing on jars of honey. How does that saying go again? Oh, yeah. Eve was a few french fries short of a happy meal. At first, I gave her the benefit of the doubt, but she didn't seem to get any smarter as the novel wore on. For example, her relationship with Caleb. You all know how the YA romance goes. You've got to have something that breaks the couple up. Eve gets into an argument with Caleb about wanting to stay with him instead of traveling to Califia (the shelter). He reasonably tells her he would like that, but since the king is after her, she would be safer at the shelter. You know what Eve does? She throws a tantrum and calls <i>him</i> selfish. -_- And that is the scene I lost all my respect for her. It was frustrating! I just wanted her to use her brain just once! That's not really asking too much is it? <br><br>Yet, somehow I was able to enjoy this book. Again, mostly thanks to the minor characters and Caleb. The ending leaves us with a cliffhanger you knew was coming. Let's just say it left me angry and leave it at that. Even stranger is that I really do want to check out the sequel. Huh.<br><br>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13048771275144870563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_299989689" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/299989689" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/299989689?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=cried-my-eyes-out">cried-my-eyes-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=gimme-the-next-book">gimme-the-next-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=hand-me-some-tissues">hand-me-some-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=surprised-i-didn-t-hate-it">surprised-i-didn-t-hate-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer299989689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16994684299560828841">To say that <i>Eve</i> surprised me would be a massive, massive understatement. The only reason I picked up this book to begin with was because I have an ARC of <i>Once</i>, <i>Eve</i>'s sequel, sitting around, and I felt bad for neglecting it. I had fairly low expectations before going into <i>Eve</i>, and quite honestly, I expected my rating at the end to be at most two or three stars, after reading some of the negative reviews that almost assured I would have a similar experience. <br/><br/>And I think it may be because of those </span>
  <span id="freeText16994684299560828841" style="display:none">To say that <i>Eve</i> surprised me would be a massive, massive understatement. The only reason I picked up this book to begin with was because I have an ARC of <i>Once</i>, <i>Eve</i>'s sequel, sitting around, and I felt bad for neglecting it. I had fairly low expectations before going into <i>Eve</i>, and quite honestly, I expected my rating at the end to be at most two or three stars, after reading some of the negative reviews that almost assured I would have a similar experience. <br /><br />And I think it may be because of those very reviews that I had an experience almost completely opposite with <i>Eve</i>. Before even opening the pages <i>Eve</i>, I expected a boring read with mediocre characters and horrible world-building, as that is what most of the negative reviews led me to believe, but instead, what I got with <i>Eve</i> was a disturbing and emotionally raw novel with great characters that made me cry a countless amount of times. I found <i>Eve</i> to be a powerful and beautifully written little novel, and it was one that punched me in the gut over and over and over again. <br /><br />In the world of <i>Eve</i>, a disastrous plague has swept the entire nation and left ninety-eight of the entire population dying. After the aftermath of the plague, and after seeing her loved ones slowly fall at the hands of the plague, Eve is brought into the School - a housing place for young girls. At the School, the girls are fed, taught, and treated to until they turn eighteen. However, a day before her graduation from the School, Eve escapes to find out what really happens to the women after they graduate. Horrified by what she finds out to be the truth, she escapes from the School in a mission to go to a place called Califia; a place where she will be safe. But how will Eve, having been sheltered and kept from the outside world almost all her life, know who to trust? <br /><br />As I am writing this review, I am struggling to find another instance where a book has had as great of an emotional impact on me as <i>Eve</i> has. In fact, upon reading the very first pages in <i>Eve</i>, I found myself tearing up. This book is about love, it is about loss, it is about moving on, and, alongside that, it is about a young girl trying to run away from her future while also escaping from a deadly plague. And it handles all of that <i>amazingly</i>. <br /><br /><blockquote>I'd once read about amputees, and how they had pains where their arms and legs used to be. Phantom limbs, they were called. I'd always thought that was the best way to describe my feelings about my mother. She was now just an ache for something I'd had lost.</blockquote><br /><br />Eve is not the smartest heroine you'll ever read about, or the strongest, and she is at times a bit selfish and difficult to like, but I just found that to be the effects of her being sheltered and monitored and lied to her entire life. She's at times naive, and she is imperfect, but she learns from her mistakes and she feels guilt for her wrong decisions, seemingly miniscule and incapable of harm to her, that, unfortunately, impacted other people's lives. Eve feels regret for those decisions she's made, and she betters herself as a person through those wrong decisions. Or, in other words, she's human. And she's a lot more of a believable character than half of the heroines in young adult dystopians on the market today. <br /><br />As well as Eve, the secondary characters, and Eve's love interest, Caleb, were incredibly likable and developed throughout the course of the novel. I have to say that my favorite character in <i>Eve</i> was Arden, and that my favorite relationship in <i>Eve</i> was the one between her and Eve. The two girls are incredibly different and not ideal friends at first, but throughout the novel they learn that they are similar in many ways, and their relationship has one of the most interesting and well-developed dynamics I've had the pleasure to read about this year. I only wish I could say the same for the relationship between the two central characters, Eve and Caleb. While I definitely found Caleb to be a likable character, and Eve an at times likable character, I was never really sold on their relationship together. It was sweet, and it wasn't insta-love, but to me it just felt like there was no basis behind the purpose of the romance. Though I guess sometimes relationships are like that in the real world, as well. <br /><br />While the novel itself is certainly not without its flaws - the biggest one pertaining to the world-building, or lack thereof, I found <i>Eve</i> to be an engaging and powerful read, set in a grisly and disturbing world that is scarily possible, and the emotional impact it had on me is one that I am sure to remember. I am now happy that I have that ARC of <i>Once</i> waiting for me, and I am eager to see what Carey has in store. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16994684299560828841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5336509941306640034"><b>
  <i>Re-read from 26th-29th Nov 2013</i>

Males and females have been saparated ever since. <br/><br/><a target='_blank' title='ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting' href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/845/1438.jpg/' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://imageshack.us' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><br/><b>“Sometimes it seems like all the things I need t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5336509941306640034" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Re-read from 26th-29th Nov 2013</i>
</b><br><br><b>“You can love anyone. Love is just caring about someone very deeply. Feeling like that person matters to you, like your whole world would be sadder without them in it.”</b><br><br><b>
  <u>GENRE: YA/DYSTOPIAN/ROMANCE (with bits of action)</u>
</b><br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/593/9xee.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385928578i/7260922.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>WHERE DO YOU GO WHEN NOWHERE IS SAFE?</blockquote>
</b><br><br><i>Eve</i> is set in the year 2032, 16 years after a deadly virus wiped out most of Earth's population. Males and females have been saparated ever since. <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/845/1438.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385928241i/7260884.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>“Sometimes it seems like all the things I need to know, I don’t. And all the things I do know are completely wrong.” </b><br><br>At the school were Eve and all the other girls lived and learned, they were taught that men can not be trusted. Men will manipulate them. Lie to them, and hurt them. Men are the enemy of every girl in New America. But everything they learned was a lie... <br> <br>Eve, a 16 year old, innocent girl, finds out the brutal truth hidden from everyone. She knows one thing...if she stays she will be doomed to an eternity of pain, sorrow and helplessness. There is not other option but to run away beyond the wall that used to be her safe haven from all the dangers out there. Now, she is alone, scared, hungry. <br> <br>Then she meets Caleb....<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/199/znxu.jpg/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385928241i/7260883._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>Caleb is a rough, rebellious boy living in the wild. Separated from men her whole life, Eve automatically doesn't trust him. But soon, Caleb wins over her trust...and eventually her heart. He promises he will protect her, but soldiers are looking for Eve.<br><br><b>And to be in love in a world like this one, is to be already cursed.<br>Sacrifices and choices have to be made...true love...or her life?</b><br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/41/w4g.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>I have first read <i>Eve</i> in Jan 2012, and LOVED it to the very last page. <br>But it's been a long time since then, and obviously my tastes in books have changed quite a lot as i haven't really enjoyed Eve this time. <br>I re-read <i>Eve</i> because i want to re-read <i>Once</i> (2nd book) so i can finally read the last one and be done with the whole trilogy.<br><br>I wonder how that's gonna work out for me.<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/69/rdn5.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>
  <u>Characters</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Eve</u>
</b> <br>Reading through my old review, i am surprised that i actually wrote i 'loved' her, because it was far from what i felt now. <br>I could not connect with Eve and i didn't like her. Wouldn't say i hated her either though.<br>To me, she was too girly, and too...dependent on someone else.<br>She couldn't do anything useful, like defend her own ass and look after herself. Everybody else had to do that for her and it got on my nerves, as many characters that i actually liked died or got hurt protecting her. <br><br><b>
  <u>Caleb</u>
</b><br>I didn't necessarily 'like' him too. He was..OK. To be honest, it felt WEIRD reading about him, and how weird is THAT?<br>He definitely did not make me swoon..or drool for that matter. <br>But i liked how...ermm...thoughtful and 'nice' he was to others. Caleb was very helpful. <br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/833/fe0r.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261712.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>“A relationship between two people can be judged by the list of things unspoken between them.” </b><br><br><b>
  <u>The relationship between Eve and Caleb</u>
</b> was perhaps the worse thing of the whole book. I felt no connection, chemistry or anything whats so ever between those two. The romance felt shallow and forced. If you're not going to take time to develop the relationship between characters step-by-step, realistically then don't even bother...like, seriously just don't.<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/689/pvpu.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261713.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><i>Eve</i> is a very emotionally action-packed book that i think many readers would enjoy, especially dystopian fans. <br>I am a sucker for action scenes and, like, running away from people plotlines, and this one had a lot of those that were actually amazing at times. But the problem was, for some reason i couldn't get into it? Maybe it was because of the style of writing (which i'm not really a big fan of).<br><br>The world building was good. I give it 6/10. Not the best i have read, but decent stuff that i liked. <br><br><b>“Love was death’s only adversary, the only thing powerful enough to combat its clawing, desperate grasp.</b><br><br>The ending was a bit like...<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/10/tfy.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261714.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br>I still found it very sad, but i didn't cry mind you.<br><br>For those who will read this for the first time you're gonna be all like...<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/833/l6i3.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a> <br><br>and some will get teared up a little...<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/607/675.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385933256ra/7261716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://imageshack.us" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><b>“I loved my mother too,' I said. 'I still do. That's the thing - it never goes away, even if the person does.”</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b> <i>Eve</i> was a good read. I liked it. <br>Would i recommend it to others? Sure, why not. I have a feeling people will like it more than i did, but <b>BE WARNED</b>, this book might creep you out a tiny bit<br><br><i>Sincerely - The Critic</i><br><br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_227207447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227207447" />
    <a title="J. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1950497-j"><img alt="J. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312295787p2/1950497.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227207447?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="J. " href="/user/show/1950497-j">J. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227207447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13188459093905415379">3.5<br/>*low whistle* WOW. There is quite a bit of ragging on this book here.<br/>I did a naughty thing. I picked this book to read, then looked at the reviews here. And did I ever TAINT my own mind!<br/>So I immediately started off wanting to hate it and call it misogynistic. But guess what? I actually DIDN'T hate it!<br/><br/>Okay, so it's not the Mona Lisa of YA, but really, I don't think it deserves the one and two star ratings.<br/><br/>Here's the biggest thing to remember about this dystopian world:<br/><b>The role of women in this</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13188459093905415379" style="display:none">3.5<br />*low whistle* WOW. There is quite a bit of ragging on this book here.<br />I did a naughty thing. I picked this book to read, then looked at the reviews here. And did I ever TAINT my own mind!<br />So I immediately started off wanting to hate it and call it misogynistic. But guess what? I actually DIDN'T hate it!<br /><br />Okay, so it's not the Mona Lisa of YA, but really, I don't think it deserves the one and two star ratings.<br /><br />Here's the biggest thing to remember about this dystopian world:<br /><b>The role of women in this society is something society-created, <u>not</u> humanity-created.</b><br />What I mean by that is that this is a dystopia for a reason. Eve, Caleb and even Leif are all products of <i>that</i> particular society.<br /><br />That being said, was Eve incredibly weak and annoying at times? Yes. Was her attitude around Caleb highly and annoying naive at times? Yes! But (and this is really true) she did everything with the best intentions.<br />Some of the worst things imaginable have started with the best intentions, but that is not the point here.<br />The point is I would judge a female character from this world acting like that harder than I judged Eve in her world.<br />AND I got say I thought she manned up there at the end. In the beginning she was deathly afraid of a man and by the end (NOT A SPOILER) she's pointing a gun at a man. AFTER all the death, etc she's seen. Come on, that takes some gutage.<br /><br />And don't get me wrong. The premise of this book is quite appalling. I wouldn't call myself a feminist by definition, but the idea of women being a baby-factory is disgusting, demeaning, degrading and morally wrong. So don't think my defense of Eve's character, etc is stemming from some hyper-traditional beliefs. It's not.<br /><br />But the story was well-written, there was good pacing, the characterization was good, and you know what? I think I will be checking out the sequel!<br />I did feel like certain things were rushed. Like her finding out about the baby-factory life, the escape and the relationship with Caleb (though I could argue myself on that one - being uber sheltered would lead to more extremist feelings when they came about).<br /><br />Okay. Off my soapbox now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13188459093905415379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1851107768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851107768" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1851107768?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1851107768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17911345829101481270">Zero stars.<br/><br/>My plan was to give this book somewhere around 2 or 2.5 stars because it was cliché, unoriginal, riddled with plot conveniences, and sloppy. I just wasn't enjoying it at all. Then I got about 3/4 of the way through when the main character was raped and the rape was blamed on her. And it never got rectified.<br/><br/>I'll keep from using names in case you plan to read this book (which I don't recommend - there wasn't a single good element in this story):<br/><br/>Rapist: "She wanted me. Not you - <i> me </i>"<br/><br/>Lov</span>
  <span id="freeText17911345829101481270" style="display:none">Zero stars.<br /><br />My plan was to give this book somewhere around 2 or 2.5 stars because it was cliché, unoriginal, riddled with plot conveniences, and sloppy. I just wasn't enjoying it at all. Then I got about 3/4 of the way through when the main character was raped and the rape was blamed on her. And it never got rectified.<br /><br />I'll keep from using names in case you plan to read this book (which I don't recommend - there wasn't a single good element in this story):<br /><br />Rapist: "She wanted me. Not you - <i> me </i>"<br /><br />Love Interest (after wrestling this guy off of her): (love interest) turned toward me, his face wrought with confusion. "Is that true?"<br /><br />Main Character: My hands trembled violently and tears streamed down my face. What (rapist) had done was wrong, And yet... I had sat beside him on the piano, playing for him. I had allowed his shoulder to press close as he spoke of his family. I had let his hand squeeze mine. Had I given him some unspoken invitation? Had my kindness seemed like something more? "I don't know," I said, covering my mouth with my hand.<br /><br />Then the love interest yells a little and runs off into the woods to pout and we get to read pages and pages of her dreaming of him, pining after him, and wishing she could just explain herself and explain that, in fact, she hadn't wanted to be raped.<br /><br />Then, when the love interest finally (and predictably) finds her and everything is made okay again, I simply couldn't find it in me to care. At all. Because if my husband ever had to pull a man off of me, that man would be dead before he ever had a chance to blame me. And if the rapist did try to blame me, there is no way my husband would even consider that anything like that could ever have been my fault. And frankly, none of that was ever fixed in the book. Everyone just moved on.<br /><br />This book wasn't good, it was getting a low rating from me anyway. But that whole situation deserved a rant. You should know what you're getting into - I don't recommend this book to anyone.</span>

<div id="review_199867215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/199867215" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285872916p2/2276205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199867215?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199867215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14285507925043512887"><i>Eve</i> by Anna Carey is light on the world-building as dystopias go. It’s not one of those books that offer an incisive commentary on some aspect of our existing culture. It’s more, “here’s a setting where things suck; now we have a backdrop for a romance/adventure story.” That’s not inherently bad. It just makes it a fluffy read, rather than a chilling one. <i>Eve</i> doesn’t possess the depth of books like Margaret Atwood’s <i>The Handmaid’s Tale</i> (which Carey quotes in the front matter) or George Orwell’s </span>
  <span id="freeText14285507925043512887" style="display:none"><i>Eve</i> by Anna Carey is light on the world-building as dystopias go. It’s not one of those books that offer an incisive commentary on some aspect of our existing culture. It’s more, “here’s a setting where things suck; now we have a backdrop for a romance/adventure story.” That’s not inherently bad. It just makes it a fluffy read, rather than a chilling one. <i>Eve</i> doesn’t possess the depth of books like Margaret Atwood’s <i>The Handmaid’s Tale</i> (which Carey quotes in the front matter) or George Orwell’s <i>1984</i> or Aldous Huxley’s <i>Brave New World</i> or Suzanne Collins’s <i>The Hunger Games</i>. Even for a just-for-fun book, though, there are aspects of <i>Eve</i>’s world-building that don’t quite make sense.<br /><br />The most jarring example is Eve’s education. Young orphan girls in Anna Carey’s “New America” are raised and educated to expect one kind of future, and then after graduation, are thrust into a completely different life than the one they were promised. This seems like an ineffective way to run an evil empire. Why do this bait and switch, which is expensive, time-consuming, pointless, and guaranteed to foster discontent? Why not just feed the girls propaganda about the life they’ll really have, selling it as a glorious mission?<br /><br />Eve escapes the fate ordained for her at school, however, and finds herself on the lam. The rest of the novel follows her as she travels the ruins of the western United States looking for a safe haven. She makes an unlikely friend in a fellow runaway student, and also meets a boy and falls in love for the first time. If you’re looking for an exciting read about a girl and a boy falling in love while running from The Man, you may enjoy <i>Eve</i>.<br /><br />For my part, though, I was irked. The illogic of the opening sequences got the book off to a bad start, and then I had issues with Eve as a character. She is a Mary Sue whose unique awesomeness is frequently touted. All the good guys love her. All the bad guys want to rape her, including the King of New America, whose obsession with a girl he’s never met is never really explained.<br /><br />We are told of Eve’s selflessness, but her selfless acts are often told briefly or pushed offscreen. The behaviors we do see are frequently naïve (though this naiveté is understandable, to an extent) and selfish. My overall impression of Eve is that she does boneheaded things and then walks away unscathed while other people pay for her mistakes. If she learns a lesson, it’s the wrong lesson. At one point, she makes a mistake late at night. In the morning, she doesn’t confess to it until the evidence is discovered. Disaster follows. When Eve reflects on it later, she thinks, “It should’ve been the first thing I said when I awoke.” Not that she shouldn’t have done it, not that she should have asked and possibly learned a safer way to achieve her goal, not that she should have fessed up right after doing it — but that she should have said something earlier <i>the following day</i>.<br /><br />The ending doesn’t seem to make much sense either. It feels, at first, like an out-of-character contrivance to create extra angst for book two. But on second thought, it fits pretty well with what we’ve seen of Eve so far. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Eve reaches safety, while her badly injured boyfriend is left to fend for himself. I think the logic is that he’ll be safer without her. There’s some merit to that, but I just keep thinking about how badly injured he is and that he is all alone. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14285507925043512887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_185126813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185126813" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185126813?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185126813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8698989809691243013"><b>2.5/5</b><br/><br/>There's potential here, but what comes to mind right now is Handmaid's Tale, even Wither. Except Eve is a pale version of those. Where all three possess elements of a society being rebuilt on the backs of unwanted, Eve lacks the deeper emotions and awareness that Handmaid's has; it also lacks the seamless, lush writing that Wither possesses. That said, Eve isn't a bad story despite some of the clumsy dialogue and sudden/abrupt shifts because right now it feels like to ended too soon. <br/><br/>Eve's </span>
  <span id="freeText8698989809691243013" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5</b><br /><br />There's potential here, but what comes to mind right now is Handmaid's Tale, even Wither. Except Eve is a pale version of those. Where all three possess elements of a society being rebuilt on the backs of unwanted, Eve lacks the deeper emotions and awareness that Handmaid's has; it also lacks the seamless, lush writing that Wither possesses. That said, Eve isn't a bad story despite some of the clumsy dialogue and sudden/abrupt shifts because right now it feels like to ended too soon. <br /><br />Eve's story starts where most stories like these do: a girl relatively happy (and ignorant) with how things are. But that's quick to change because after seeing how things are going to be, she runs... and finds herself in a place where she does not know what to do, with a vague goal of getting somewhere else. <br /><br />And I think this is where my problems with Eve start. Everything is so vague. Her world, her history is bare, I knew little of it and what little that is known is still too bare (for my liking.) That after a plague destroyed nearly everything, rebuilding was done mainly through those orphaned. That while girls were broodmares, boys labored. That while they toiled, a new City was built, protected by soldiers of a New America. Of course there were those too old or too opposed, but we got little exposure of them. In the end? I simply wanted to see more than Caleb and Eve's love develop (which did develop. And I'm not saying that this development was a bad thing becasue, at least there was something tackled beyond a glance.) <br /><br />World building is thin. Like Eve, we no little of what was and know even less about what is. Character development also leaves a lot desired. Both these could have been tackled a bit more. The parts that are absolutely clear is that there's a girl on the run with a boy who knows a bit more than she does. Their companionship goes to the next stage. A lot of chasing and an ending that's not happy but designed to push through to the sequel. As I said, while Eve is far from perfect, there's potential here, so much so that I'm likely to read the rest.<br /><br />*Thanks NetGalley!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8698989809691243013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
